## Domain Knowledge (LLM-generated)
**Domain**: chemical reaction kinetics
**Analysis**: This is a chemical reaction kinetics problem where we seek the rate law dA/dt as a function of concentration A and time t. Classical rate laws express the reaction rate as a function of reactant concentration, with possible explicit time dependence for non-autonomous systems (e.g., photolysis, varying temperature).

**Common formula structures in this domain**:
- Zero-order kinetics: dA_dt = c0 (constant rate, independent of concentration)
- First-order kinetics: dA_dt = c0 * A (rate proportional to concentration, radioactive decay, unimolecular reactions)
- Second-order kinetics: dA_dt = c0 * A**2 (bimolecular reaction of same species)
- nth-order kinetics: dA_dt = c0 * A**c1 (general power-law rate dependence)
- Reversible first-order: dA_dt = c0 * A + c1 (first-order with equilibrium offset, A ↔ B)
- Michaelis-Menten type: dA_dt = c0 * A / (c1 + A) (enzyme kinetics, saturation kinetics)
- Substrate inhibition: dA_dt = c0 * A / (c1 + A + c2 * A**2) (enzyme kinetics with inhibition)
- Mixed-order kinetics: dA_dt = c0 * A + c1 * A**2 (competing first and second order pathways)
- Autocatalytic: dA_dt = c0 * A * (c1 + c2 * A) (autocatalytic reaction network)
- Langmuir-Hinshelwood: dA_dt = c0 * A / (c1 + A)**2 (surface catalysis kinetics)
- Time-dependent first-order: dA_dt = c0 * A * exp(c1 * t) (time-varying rate constant, e.g., temperature ramp)
- Parallel pathway: dA_dt = c0 * A**c1 + c2 * A**c3 (multiple simultaneous reaction pathways)
- Cooperative kinetics (Hill): dA_dt = c0 * A**c1 / (c2 + A**c1) (cooperative binding/reaction)
- Fractional order with offset: dA_dt = c0 * A**c1 + c2 (fractional order kinetics with constant source/sink)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Pure concentration dependence (no explicit time) → autonomous ODE rate law, suggests closed chemical system with fixed conditions
- Rate proportional to integer power of A → elementary reaction step with molecularity equal to the power
- Rational function of A (saturation form) → enzyme-catalyzed or surface-catalyzed reaction with limited active sites
- Negative rate values (dA_dt < 0) with magnitude increasing with A → consumption reaction where reactant is being depleted
- Linear relationship dA_dt vs A with nonzero intercept → reversible first-order reaction approaching equilibrium or constant production term
- Rate that changes sign at some concentration → equilibrium point exists, reversible reaction with competing forward/backward rates
- Explicit time dependence in rate → non-isothermal conditions, photochemical forcing, or catalyst deactivation over time
- Product of A with (1-A/c) form → logistic-type kinetics suggesting autocatalysis with finite carrying capacity
- Square root or fractional power of A → chain reaction mechanism or dissociative adsorption kinetics
- Rate expression with A in denominator → inhibition by reactant itself or competitive adsorption effects
